★ AUTOLOOP LIVE · 10 AUTONOMOUS CYCLES SHIPPED JUN 28 2026 · DAY 169 · v14.0 DESIGN-SYSTEM REVENUE ENGINE SCOPED EIN RE-FAXED TO IRS · RECEIVE LINE LIVE

The machine now builds itself overnight · Autoloop shipped 10 autonomous cycles. Design-System revenue engine scoped on the Jun 27-28 founder call · EIN re-faxed to the IRS on a live send/receive line.

Day 169 opens the autonomy era. The Oraya Autoloop went live Jun 27 and has shipped 10 verified cycles — the opt-in capture page, the homeowner outreach package, a 77-lead Lob mail-merge, the zero-gate B2B HR lane, and a fill-once cross-lane config — while catching a dead ATTOM key on its own. The Design-System Revenue Engine is the new go-to-market: SMB voice-AI deals (~$1k recurring each) + websites from $300, sold through one multi-product Meta ad → free demo → G-Meet close, on a $500 / 50-50 / micro-campaign test. Cinematic demo v3 hybrid spec locked; EIN re-faxed to the IRS on a live send/receive line (reply expected ~8 days). Voice stack steady at Outbound v128 + Inbound v15. The company's only bottleneck is now 5 founder approvals — every lane underneath them is built.

✨ What's new · Jun 8-28 sweep (since v13.0) — May sweep preserved below
  • 🤖 ORAYA AUTOLOOP LIVE — the machine now builds itself overnight (10 cycles, Jun 27-28). A headless claude -p prompt-loop (launchd, 09:00 + 21:00 PT) with goals / state / guardrails now runs autonomously and ships a verified, reversible deliverable each cycle. Built so far: the TCPA opt-in capture page (07_optin_landing/), the homeowner outreach package (08_outreach/ — zero-TCPA direct-mail postcard + CAN-SPAM email sequence), a Lob mail-merge CSV (77 TIER1 California leads, 77/77 mailable, a per-lead QR so a booked appointment is attributable to the exact mailing), the B2B layoff→HR referral lane (09_b2b_hr_lane/ — the only lane that can go live with NONE of the spend / compliance gates), and a fill-once cross-lane launch-config that stamps 20 shared tokens into all three lanes from one .env. It self-audits with real evidence (parses its own output, aborts on drift) and caught a dead ATTOM key on its own. Blueprint: oraya-autoloop/ORAYA_AUTONOMY_BLUEPRINT.md.
  • 💰 DESIGN-SYSTEM REVENUE ENGINE locked — the new go-to-market (Jun 27-28 call). The design system stops being an internal tool and becomes the product. Two revenue lines: (a) autonomous / voice-AI systems sold to small-to-medium businesses — "one 1,000-2,000-minute voice deal = ~$1,000 recurring from a single client"; (b) high-graphic websites + ad creative spun out of the design system — entry price $300 (vs $500-600 in the open market), buildable in ~1 hour. Channel: one multi-product Meta / Facebook ad (voice + Claude-Code systems + websites) → free demo / trial / pilot → G-Meet close with both founders. Budget: $500 to start, split 50/50, run as ~6 micro-campaigns at ~$3/day, optimise at day 10-15, pour budget into the winners. "Meta does ~80% of the targeting now — we are the agency."
  • 🧮 AD-AGENT skill queued — so spend never runs haywire. Build an ad-running agent inside the Claude system that creates the creative from the design system and targets only searches relevant to our products, so the $500 test reaches only people actively looking. Boatman deferred ~2 weeks (needs ~$2k to start) — the design-system ad path is the cheaper, faster lane right now (starts at ~$200-300) and runs in parallel.
  • 🎬 CINEMATIC DEMO v3 — hybrid spec locked. After reviewing demos #1 and #2 line-by-line on the call: take the intro + ending (particles converging on the "Oraya" mark) + music bed from demo #2, the animated website pop-ups / tech visuals from demo #1, and add word-by-word subtitles — bigger, bolder, on a translucent dark rectangle (YouTube / Instagram style) so the visuals still read through. The autonomous agent is tasked to generate demo v3 overnight from this meeting's transcript; founders then criticise it as if it were a live Meta ad before it ships to the site + ads.

  • 🎤 Opener reframe SHIPPED — Outbound v128 LIVE (May 29). The Greetings part 2 STEP 1 opener was leading with a mortgage-protection mechanism lecture ("Mortgage protection is simple: you pay a small monthly premium…") AND asking for the appointment in the same breath — telegraphing the pitch, so cold 15-month-old leads bailed. Reframed via 3 surgical edits: now LEADS with the property flag ("Your property on {{address}} came up flagged as having no mortgage protection on the loan with {{lender}}"), disarms the old lead ("this was a while back, no worries if you don't remember"), explicitly says "I'm not going to pitch you anything on this call," and ends with an open question to build interest — the appointment ask is deferred to the adaptive paths once they engage. PATHs A–G, pain hook, and NEPQ connector preserved. Day 169 deep state · full essay · carry-overs from v13.0 / v12.0 / v11.4 / v11.3

Jun 28 state (Day 169, Sun) — the autonomy era opens. The story of June is that Oraya stopped needing a human in the loop to make progress. The Oraya Autoloop — a headless claude -p driver with a goals / state / guardrails file set and a launchd cadence (09:00 + 21:00 PT) — went live Jun 27 and has run 10 cycles, each shipping a verified, reversible deliverable and writing back its own evidence. It built the consumer funnel end-to-end on the Claude side: the TCPA opt-in capture page (07_optin_landing/), the homeowner outreach package (08_outreach/ — a zero-TCPA direct-mail postcard plus a CAN-SPAM email sequence), a Lob-shaped mail-merge of the 77 TIER1 California leads (77/77 mailable, each carrying a QR that makes a booked appointment attributable to the exact mailing), the B2B layoff→HR referral lane (09_b2b_hr_lane/ — chosen precisely because it can launch with none of the consumer spend / compliance gates), and a fill-once launch-config that stamps 20 shared tokens into all three lanes from a single .env. Along the way it pressure-tested its own promises (proving it cannot run Apollo unattended, then making the contact-pull founder-executable) and corrected the source of truth when it found the ATTOM trial key returning 401. The net effect: every lane is now built, merge-ready and compliance-checked, and the company's entire forward motion reduces to five founder approvals — launch the B2B HR lane, fund + approve the Lob postcard, fill the launch values once, refresh the ATTOM key, fund BatchData.

The Design-System Revenue Engine (Jun 27-28 founder call). The strategic pivot of the month: the in-house design system becomes the revenue product, not just the thing that makes the dashboards pretty. Two lines were locked. First, autonomous / voice-AI systems sold to small-and-medium businesses — a single 1,000-2,000-minute voice deal is ~$1,000 of recurring revenue from one client, and the design system creates its own ad. Second, high-graphic websites and ad creative produced from the design system at a $300 entry price (against $500-600 in the open market) and a build time of roughly an hour — aimed at both the "mediocre existing website" buyer and the "rolled my own with Claude" buyer, neither of whom can reach this level of design. The channel is one multi-product Meta / Facebook ad (voice + Claude-Code systems + websites, so a single click can match any of several intents) into a free demo / trial / pilot, converted on a G-Meet with both founders present. The spend model is deliberately small and empirical: $500 to start, split 50/50, fanned across ~6 micro-campaigns at ~$3/day, with budget reallocated to whatever converts by day 10-15 — the same "Meta does 80% of the targeting, we are the agency" logic the founders adopted for dealerships, now pointed at our own systems. An ad-agent skill is queued so the creative is generated and the targeting kept tight automatically. Boatman is deferred ~2 weeks (it needs ~$2k to start); this path starts at ~$200-300 and runs first.

Cinematic demo v3, the portfolio, and the EIN. The founders reviewed two cuts of the launch film side-by-side and converged on a hybrid: intro + ending (particles converging on the Oraya mark) + music bed from cut #2, the animated website pop-ups and tech visuals from cut #1, and word-by-word subtitles on a translucent dark rectangle so the captions read without hiding the visuals — with the autonomous agent tasked to generate demo v3 overnight from the call transcript. A "Made by Oraya" portfolio is being assembled as credibility-by-product — orayalabs.ai, the demo, the sister's Enviroplan carbon-capture / orbit-restoration NGO (Durham Venture School in September) and Bloomgrass, plus client sites. And after the May certified-mail SS-4 never arrived, the founders stood up a RedFax send/receive line (510-497-1224) on the call and faxed the 3-page SS-4 to the IRS EIN fax (855-641-6935), confirmed delivered in 101 seconds; because the form now carries a receiving fax number, the EIN can come back by fax in roughly 8 business days instead of 2-3 weeks — clearing the last A2P blocker onto the fast track.

May 28 state (Day 138, Thu) — "Launch Week" closes. The two voice agents Oraya has been forging for six weeks — outbound mortgage-protection and inbound life/health triage — both crossed the publish line on the same day. Outbound v126 ships the email digit-word → numeric-digit fix Maya kept biting on (callers saying "john wick one two at gmail dot com" now store as johnwick12@gmail.com rather than the literal word string) and inherits v125's appointment_timestamp ISO 8601 rewrite + v124's callback_scheduled_time role separation. Inbound v15 collapses all three of those patches into a single publish so the inbound and outbound flows now run on identical extraction logic, ending six weeks of drift. Both backends — calendar event creation, opt-in confirmation email, SMS, DNC harvest, admin log dispatch — verified on a live test call (May 27 1:39 AM, caller "Adrian Marino", appointment slot Thu May 28 11 AM landed end-to-end). Pre-publish bug found same day: inbound had been mistakenly wired to the OUTBOUND backend — that's why test calls produced 10 emails per call. Cause was the form-submit fan-out path; it now routes to its own inbound post-call workflow.

REAL ESTATE PROJECT (P3) scoped end-to-end on the May 27-28 founder call. Day-trading agent scratched (Chitraksh has back-tested for 3 years, the strategies don't translate to live execution — revenue potential lower than insurance / real-estate / voice). Real Estate is the "perfect next step": the lead-gen muscle being built for P2 Insurance transplants directly into P3 Real Estate — same enrichment, same outreach, different buyer side. Two human channels: (a) Art Yano — CA licensed broker, family runs a property-management company, auctions houses for investors at $10K-$50K per wholesale, currently taking time away from real estate to care for his terminally-ill mother ($5-10K / month in home medical for dialysis + multiple treatments) so a system that does the prospecting / pricing / blast for him is timely; (b) Frankie's mom — licensed CA real-estate agent + broker, retiring, wants a position alongside Art. The buyer side is NOT consumer end-buyers — it's investors / flippers (the 99% of this market). The system scrapes Facebook + investor sites for CA flippers, enriches, ingests to our database. When a seller signs an off-market contract (e.g., hoarder house that won't sell on Zillow as-is), we blast that deal simultaneously to 50+ investors in the database with full underwriting metrics: comparables (1-2 mi radius, same vintage), rehab estimate, post-rehab ARV, days-on-market in that ZIP, urgency timer, GPS, photos, pie chart of cost-vs-profit — "everything an investor needs to decide in 60 seconds." Investor responds → we wholesale the contract → $10-50K spread per close. Tech visual reference is the Oraya site clone Chitraksh already built ("Turn difficult property distributions into clear" with dropdown CTAs — "Inherited a property / Going through divorce / …"). Sequencing: P2 insurance lead-gen ships first → learnings flow into P3 real-estate. Frankie's frame: "Now we don't have to do anything but refining and honing in and hyper-focusing on system feedback loops — we're good for the rest of the year."

Lead-Gen Dashboard wired into top-bar navigation. The standalone INSURANCE_LEADGEN_DASHBOARD.html (which Chitraksh has been iterating on as the operational state-of-the-data-side) is now linked as a violet button in the top-bar of this main HQ dashboard. ATTOM (key in .oraya-credentials/, verified working), BatchData (configured, needs OAuth reconnect), and PropertyRadar (needs a US phone number from Frankie) are the three enrichment lanes already wired into the lead-gen agent. $60 bake-off queued: $20 each across all three providers, compare data quality + actual outreach conversion, pick the winner before scaling spend. Property Shark / CoreLogic / TruePeopleSearch deferred behind this test.

"AI Employees / AI CEO" master-vision committed (May 27, 12:35 AM). Voice AI is now explicitly the wedge, not the destination. After the wedge converts, the upsell stack is: (i) lead-gen + follow-up infrastructure (the dashboard the client uses daily); (ii) a team of AI employees — one per workflow surface (calendar, mail, SMS, post-call, KB, finance); (iii) an AI CEO over the employees that gives directions to real humans (call, email, SMS), not just to sub-agents. The moat = stickiness — the more workflow surfaces we embed, the harder it is for the client to extract us, same pattern as bundled telecom / bundled insurance. "You could sell them a team of fucking employees, you could sell them an infrastructure, and then you can sell them a CEO to manage their infrastructure." — Frankie. Order of deploy: P2 insurance lead-gen → P3 real-estate lead-gen → per-client AI-employee stack → per-client AI-CEO.

v11.4 carry-over (May 19 "Voice-Fix + Sales-Master Week" close). The week reframed Oraya's voice surface from "agent feels almost there" to "agent passes the founder ear test." Maya/Tessa on the inbound life/health triage agent had been producing a "creature" artifact mid-sentence on test calls — voice cutting out, muffling, partial syllables; recording came back clean every time which told us it was a runtime transport issue, not a generation issue. The May 18 02:09-02:21 call session ran the diagnostic live with Frankie on speaker: tried voice swap (got worse), then identified that voices are Cartesia imports (not native Retell), which means the variable in scope is Cartesia ↔ Retell transport, not Retell-internal config. Three changes shipped in one pass: (a) Voice volume +166 (was at default, agent was simply speaking too quietly for the cellphone codec to render mid-sentence breath), (b) Interruption-sensitivity reduced to floor (agent was treating its own breath / silence frames as a user barge-in and clipping), (c) Background-noise removal turned ON. Bonus: voice-speed toggle, which was ON in two nodes but OFF globally, brought to OFF everywhere for consistency. Sonic 3 model swapped for Sonic 3.5 — default was sticking to the more-stable older release; experimental newer release turned out to be more stable in our case. Post-fix call: "It's 100% better." — Frankie.

Sales-master script rebuild. With the voice transport fixed, the script bottleneck surfaced — the agent sounded "robotic because it's a script." Decision: don't rewrite the script line-by-line in our weaker voices, instead let Claude HQ merge five sales GOATs into a single prompt: Jeremy Miner (NPQ — neuro-emotional persuasion questions; statements-as-questions removed), Jordan Belfort (straight-line: tonality + control), Chris Voss (tactical empathy + mirror + label), Andy Albright (mortgage-protection 30-day frame, "reason for the call is non-negotiable"), Alex Hormozi (loss-aversion 2.5× — humans hate loss 2.5× more than they love gain — reframe "family loses the house in 30 days" not "family gets a payment"). Trigger updated from death to death OR disabling illness / can't work. Sam Lair upfront contract baked in: "If by the end of five minutes this isn't a fit, you'll tell me — deal?" — reframes the no, gives caller permission to exit, lowers defense. Pitch bullet ordering locked: are-you-familiar-with-MP → (yes/no, same response) → explain trigger + payout → one / two / three / six-month time-to-decide → keep / rent / sell. "Most people will say yes even if they don't know" — the question is rhetorical and is there to anchor authority + create permission to teach.

n8n single-prompt agent fork. Even with the GOAT-merge in the node-based architecture, the agent kept showing seams. Decision (May 19, 03:25): fork the agent into a single-prompt architecture, hand Claude HQ the full extracted context from the existing tree (already in scope via Retell API tokens), let it author the script natively. Node version preserved as fallback. New pre-filled form delivered: orayacorporation.app.n8n.cloud/form/7811db04-a919-425a-972f-39cb36953ff8 — one submit button, phone pre-filled, instant ring — built specifically for Frankie's testing loop ("record myself doing it so I don't have to write hella shit down, drop you a video").

"In Sync" daily-block schedule locked. Evening: optional, both founders open but no fixed slot. India side: 4:30 AM PT = 5:00 PM IST; 10 AM-1 PM PT = 10:30 PM-1:30 AM IST — Chitraksh's "I sleep late anyway" window. Goes on shared calendar as recurring, notifications + automations on top. Frankie: "Once we agree on set times, hopefully we can do 30 min to 90 min meetings, twice a day."

IRS / EIN status. EIN is the last A2P blocker. Frankie's first EIN was issued over the phone in one call — IRS gating this one because Frankie already has one on file, and that's the only theory. May 19 02:33 AM the call went on hold; ends with "they don't open till 8 AM" which is Frankie's day-job start. Plan: Chitraksh runs the AM call rotation from India while Frankie's on the road, Frankie picks up post-day-job. Email draft to IRS staged in parallel. GHL stays organization-owned (cannot be individual); campaign registers on Frankie's personal path with Oraya relationship fully disclosed in privacy + ToS — the canonical sole-prop A2P pattern, approval-likely.

Texas-homeowner lead lane. Research closed May 18 02:28. California is the worst US state to launch cold-data outreach in: CA Delete Act + CCPA + CA-specific consumer-protection act create such tight enrichment liability that no major consumer-data platform will sell enriched CA new-homeowner records. Texas is the inverse — no equivalent state-level act, enrichment platforms openly sell. Plan: scrape Texas new-homeowner records (county recorder + state property data sets) → enrich via consumer-data vendors (B2B enrichers like Hunter won't cut it; need consumer-side: Property Shark / CoreLogic / Atom / TruePeopleSearch class) → outbound voice + email. 4-5 page strategy doc ordered + NotebookLM-style audio podcast for founder listen (Frankie: "That was fire bro, please do that").

Claude rate-limit outage. Anthropic-side server pressure May 19 03:39, "rate limit reached retrying in 32 seconds" for 6-7 minutes. Not a Paperclip-stack-resolvable issue (that solves Cowork sandbox limits, not API server load). Multi-model fallback rule reinforced: ChatGPT + Gemini on shadow. Storage-full on current Mac blocks running 5 sub-agents locally — Mac Mini procurement is now critical-path not nice-to-have. Mac Mini timing: back-end of month, paid on Frankie's card via amazon.in, Chitraksh adding monitor to the order.

Claude Max plan downgrade. Card charged ~$100-120 this cycle. Founders aligned on $30 Claude + $30 ChatGPT next cycle — multi-vendor + halved spend. Tokens left in this cycle will be burned on Claude HQ first; sub-agents already plug into Claude HQ token pool so no architectural change required at downgrade time. Frankie: "Either way it's fine because we'll not let those tokens get wasted."

This unblocks the workflow where Claude HQ edits the agent / dashboard while the founders are still talking on the call. Frankie: "You see 03:49 — it's two minutes delay. Wow."

PROJECT P3 · SCOPED MAY 27-28 · STARTS AFTER P2’s FIRST DOLLAR

Real Estate — the $10K–$50K-per-deal machine

Plain English: a seller gives us one month to sell their house off-market. Our system instantly packages the deal — comparable sales, repair estimate, resale value, urgency timer — and blasts it to 50+ cash investors at once. First investor to say yes wins; Oraya keeps a $10K–$50K spread. Art Yano (broker) and Frankie’s mom (agent, retiring) are the human channels.

Real Estate · P3 · Investor-Flip Wholesale Lane · Art Yano + Mom (scoped May 27-28)

🏘

Real Estate Project (P3) — scoped on the May 27-28 founder call

P3 replaces the previously-floated day-trading agent (Chitraksh: 3 years of back-testing — strategies don't translate to live execution — revenue potential lower than insurance / real-estate / voice). Real Estate is the perfect next step because the lead-gen muscle being built for P2 Insurance transplants directly into the buyer side here. Two human channels in place (Art Yano + Frankie's mom), one tech-buyer focus (investors / flippers, not consumer end-buyers), one revenue model (off-market wholesale spread, $10K-$50K / close). Sequencing: P2 ships first → learnings flow into P3.

👨‍💼 The two human channels

  • Art Yano — CA licensed real-estate broker; family runs a property-management company overseeing condo, apartment, and house portfolios; personally auctions houses for investors at $10K-$50K per wholesale (no rehab, just contract-spread). Currently away from real estate taking care of his terminally-ill mother (~$5-10K / month in home medical care — dialysis, multiple treatments) — so a system that does the prospecting / pricing / blast for him is timely. Frankie's prior real-estate transaction was wholesaled by Art's circle (paid Frankie $10K because he didn't know the going rate was $30-50K, validating both the opportunity size and the asymmetric-information problem this platform solves).
  • Frankie's mom — licensed CA real-estate agent + broker, retiring, wants a position alongside Art. Friends with Art, both brokers, family-trust relationship already exists. P3 is also the structured way to financially set her up post-retirement.

🏘 Buyer side — investors / flippers, NOT consumer end-buyers

  • This vertical is 99% investor, not the wife-and-kids end-buyer. End-buyers are the wrong cohort for off-market wholesale — they want the home pretty, not the home cheap-and-cash-now.
  • Investor cohort: people who put $20-100K down per house, fix in 30-90 days, list for retail, keep $100-300K spread.
  • They want one thing: be first to see the deal, get the underwriting in 60 seconds, lock the contract before the next investor sees it. They have the cash. They have the rehab crew. They have the listing crew. They don't have the scaled-deal-flow.
  • Hedge funds already do this with data + systems. Independent investors do not yet. That's the gap.

💾 Step 1 · Build the investor database

  • Scrape Facebook + dedicated real-estate-investor sites for public real-estate-investor profiles in CA.
  • Enrich the database (same playbook as P2 insurance lead-gen: ATTOM / BatchData / TruePeopleSearch class).
  • Onboard each investor with a one-off VA-driven introductory call ("we're launching this, here's what it does, you get first-look on deals matching your buy-box") — using the Philippines call-center pattern Frankie has flagged repeatedly.

📚 Step 2 · Lock the contract (seller side)

  • Art / Mom (or future VAs) cold-call sellers: "give me one month with your house — if I can sell it for X, you'll have your money; if I can't, the contract cancels, no harm done."
  • Backed by counsel (Chitraksh + legal-stack): first-up right-to-action / lien on house if seller breaks deal.
  • Contract signed → trigger fires → auto-package the deal for investor blast.

⚡ Step 3 · Investor blast (the system)

  • Single deal goes to 50+ matched investors at once.
  • Each investor receives, on one screen: address (GPS pinned), comparables (1-2 mi radius, same vintage / sqft), photos, rehab estimate, post-rehab ARV, days-on-market in that ZIP, urgency countdown.
  • Pie chart: cost + rehab vs market ARV vs spread.
  • First-responder gets priority. Wholesale spread = $10K-$50K per close (Frankie's mid-range range, validated from his prior transaction and Art's running history).

🎨 Tech / UI demo already exists — reference visual

Chitraksh built a working visual reference during a prior session — an Oraya-site clone repositioned for property distributions ("Turn difficult property distributions into clear") with dropdown CTAs "Inherited a property / Going through divorce / …". Frankie reaction (May 27): "It's crazy, bro." — locked as the visual reference for the P3 surface. Single-prompt agent (forked + archived from the P2 push) becomes the architecture for the P3 investor-blast agent so the prompt-driven cohort matching can iterate weekly.

⚠ Adversarial-investor protection

Real-estate investors are a shady cohort by default — once they have the seller's address, a fraction will try to back-channel directly to the seller to undercut Oraya's spread ("hey, how much are they trying to give you? I'll give you 10K more."). Mitigation: legal-binding contract before the address goes out + first-up right-to-action / lien clause so any breakage by the seller pulls the spread back to Oraya. Counsel-wired into the workflow, not bolted on after.

📊 Why the lead-gen muscle transplants directly

P2 Insurance is teaching us: scrape → enrich → outreach → opt-in → voice qualifier → humans close. P3 Real Estate uses the same pipeline, just swap: scrape investors not homeowners; enrich differently (Facebook + investor sites > ATTOM); outreach by deal-blast not single-message; opt-in is implicit (investor already signed up); voice qualifier becomes the deal-blast agent. Frankie: "Once you understand the lead generation from insurance, then you apply that for the real estate — we're done. We don't have to do anything but refine and hyper-focus on feedback loops."

⛩ Sequencing · what blocks P3 from starting today

  • (1) P2 Insurance lead-gen must produce its first dollar. Without that signal, we can't reinvest cash into the P3 investor-database build.
  • (2) Art's bandwidth. Mother's illness is consuming his focus; we won't push him into a co-build until he signals readiness. Mom + the platform can pre-build the pipeline so he plugs in when he's ready.
  • (3) The investor-blast agent itself. Single-prompt architecture already archived from the P2 fork — ports cleanly. The custom UI (deal cards + comparables + countdowns) is the actual build.
  • (4) Counsel-blessed seller contract template with first-up-right-of-action / lien-on-breach clauses.

💰 Unit economics (Frankie's running numbers)

  • $10K-$50K per close as a wholesale spread (validated from Frankie's prior transaction + Art's history).
  • Art alone (no system): 2-3 houses / month → $20-150K / month gross. At scale (with the system): 5-10 houses / month is the lever — the rate-limit is contract-velocity, not buyer-velocity (investors will always say yes if the underwriting is clean).
  • Long-arc: the next layer is hedge-fund-grade signal — "house just listed in this ZIP at $X under comp, 47% chance of closing in 14 days based on last 30 ZIP-level comps." That's the moat once we have buyer-side data.

💬 Frankie verbatim · the master vision once P3 ships

"You just gave me a brilliant idea. After we're up and rolling, bro, we could fucking sell employees. Like that's the whole thing. You could sell them a team of fucking employees. Yeah. You could sell them an infrastructure, and then you can sell them a CEO to manage their infrastructure." — May 27 12:35 AM. Voice = wedge. Lead-gen = first upsell. AI employees = second upsell. AI CEO over real humans = the third. P2 insurance + P3 real estate are the two verticals where we prove the pattern on ourselves before selling it externally.

🔥 The $60 bake-off — current decision queue

Three enrichment providers are wired into the lead-gen agent (ATTOM, BatchData, PropertyRadar). Rather than commit to any one before knowing real cost-per-quality-lead, the plan is a $20-each bake-off ($60 total risk): pull the same set of TX new-homeowners across all three, compare enrichment quality, run outreach on each cohort, measure conversion. Winner scales; losers stay as fallback. Property Shark / CoreLogic / TruePeopleSearch deferred behind this test.

📍 Why Texas first (not California)

  • California has CA Delete Act + CCPA + state-specific consumer-protection laws — no major consumer-data platform will sell enriched CA new-homeowner records because the lawsuit exposure is too high.
  • Texas has no equivalent state-level act — enrichers openly sell. Bigger volume, cleaner data, no platform-side risk premium.
  • 4-5 page strategy doc + NotebookLM podcast already produced (May 21) — Frankie: "You never cease to amaze me."

🏠 Why homeowners (not laid-off workers)

  • Homeowners convert 3-5× better than laid-off workers (data + industry consensus).
  • Mortgage origination is a forcing-function trigger event: someone just signed up for a 30-year liability without protection on it.
  • Laid-off cohort is the B2B angle — contact HR / Benefits at the layoffing employer, not the worker. 2-hop expensive, only worth it once homeowner lane is humming.

🎲 Funnel map · top to bottom (live state May 28)

  1. Trigger data — WARN (live), ATTOM (live), BatchData (configured), PropertyRadar (configured), FCRA prescreen (not started), SEC Form 4 (queued), SBA loans (queued).
  2. Enrichment — BatchData skip-trace, Versium consumer-email append, AtData — bake-off pending.
  3. Outreach — Lob/PostGrid direct mail (zero TCPA risk) AND Smartlead cold email (CAN-SPAM). Voice outreach gated on EIN + A2P.
  4. Opt-in capture — landing page with TrustedForm + Jornaya certificates (TCPA PEWC).
  5. CRM — GoHighLevel sub-account (scaffolded; not yet provisioned).
  6. Voice qualifier — LIVE: Retell v126 outbound + v15 inbound (Frankie / Maya).
  7. Post-call — LIVE: calendar, email, SMS, DNC, admin log dispatch (n8n insurance post-call workflow).
  8. Licensed producer closes — Frankie (CA # 4276736 / NPN # 20996126).

⚠ Compliance blockers (must clear before consumer outreach starts)

  1. CA Data Broker registration ($6K/yr, cppa.ca.gov/data_brokers) — $200/day late penalty, Strike Force active.
  2. TX Data Broker registration (TX SOS).
  3. TX SB 140 telephone-solicitor registration ($200 + $10K bond — needed for TX SMS unless opt-in is airtight).
  4. TCPA counsel red-team ($3-5K, one-time).
  5. Privacy policy + Do-Not-Sell-or-Share page (Termly / Osano / OneTrust).
  6. CCPA Risk Assessment documented.
  7. CA producer license # in every marketing email (Cal Ins Code §1725.5(c)) — SHIPPED May 22 (CA # 4276736 + NPN # 20996126 in all backend mail/SMS templates).

📝 Decisions made (so we don't re-litigate)

  • Homeowners over laid-off (3-5× conversion delta).
  • Texas over California (enrichment availability + lawsuit risk).
  • Direct mail = parallel channel, not fallback (zero TCPA risk).
  • FCRA prescreen = separate legal track that bypasses consent requirements — pursue in parallel.
  • Hunter.io is B2B-only, does NOT return consumer emails — use Versium / AtData / LexisNexis instead.
  • CA is the binding compliance constraint — design for CA, the other 3 states are subsets.
  • Pivoted away from PropertyRadar-Python-only in favor of ATTOM (free key) + BatchData (configured). PropertyRadar Python script kept for reference.

📚 Errors corrected from earlier plans

  • The FCC "1-to-1 consent rule" was vacated by the 11th Circuit on Jan 24, 2025. The FCC repealed it. Do not build to it.
  • There was no August 2025 reinstatement of any TCPA rule. PEWC remains under pre-existing FCC rules (47 CFR §64.1200).
  • No fixed federal consent-retention period exists. TCPA SOL is 4 years; most operators retain 5-7 years for safety.
  • No fixed SBA dollar threshold for mandatory life insurance — it's lender discretion based on "key person" dependency.

Daily Sync · "In Sync" schedule + 90-min blocks (locked May 19)

♻

"In Sync" — daily founder sync, calendared, automated

Frankie pitched the In Sync naming personally as "very marketable, very very very high leverage once you get there" — named after the American boy band, weaponized for Oraya's operating cadence. Locked structure: two daily blocks, no evening fixed, no missed meetings. Goes on shared calendar as recurring with notifications + automations on top. "If me and you could be in sync with each other in our schedules — we don't miss each other anymore because now we adjust around the schedule. Everything else will adjust around my kids, I'll adjust around my sleep patterns." — Frankie, May 19 03:44.

🌚 Block 1 · 4:30 AM PT · FIXED · Recap + Plan

  • Duration: 15-30 min hard cap.
  • Format: recap yesterday → plan today.
  • India side: 5:00 PM IST — Chitraksh's prime hours.
  • CA side: right before Frankie's day-job start window (he starts 5-9 AM since the May restructure).
  • Voice / face: voice when Frankie's on the road, face when he's home.
  • Why this slot wins: earliest "latest case scenario" Frankie can hold — "the earliest I can meet on my end so that we can just kind of have an understanding".
  • Frankie verbatim: "So 4:30 should just be like recap of what the day before and what the plan of the day is. Correct. Yeah, exactly. So it can be 15 to 30 minutes, whatever. That's perfect. It doesn't matter because at that point we are just planning what we are going to get done today."

☀ Block 2 · 10 AM-1 PM PT · FLOATING · Execution

  • Duration: 60+ min, can stretch to 90 min (Frankie's preferred max focus block).
  • Window: 10 AM-1 PM PT — pick by both founders' availability that morning.
  • Why floating: Frankie has variable mid-day obligations; Chitraksh's family is wrapping the day at 12 AM-1 AM IST so cannot pre-commit a fixed time at his end.
  • India side: 10:30 PM-1:30 AM IST — Chitraksh's "I sleep late anyway" window.
  • Use: the deep work block — agent edits, dashboard pushes, GHL config, sales-script rebuilds, compliance pass-throughs.
  • Chitraksh: "At that time usually my family is going up to sleep. So sometimes I might need to attend to them — let's not fix that one."

🎌 "In Sync" branding logic · why the name was reserved

Frankie's own framing — not a metaphor, an asset thesis. "Have you ever heard of a music group called *NSYNC, the American music group? They were when I was a kid — pop singers, boy band. The name In Sync is very marketable, very very very high leverage once you get there." The name doubles as: (a) the operating cadence between the two founders, (b) a future product surface (think: founder-pair sync tools, automation-paired calendars), (c) the Oraya brand-adjacent positioning narrative when we open the kimono on how two-person AI-only companies actually operate.

⏲ 90-min block doctrine (carry-forward from May 17 02:04)

  • Frankie May 17 02:04: "Now that your schedule is free let's start working in blocks — 90 min hyper-focused blocks with executive summary and focus points + topics for each meeting so we are more productive. I want to work 2-3 90-min blocks a day."
  • Default cadence: 2-3 blocks / day · each one preceded by a written exec summary + topic list · ended with a written hand-off so the next block doesn't context-thrash.
  • Block 1 (4:30 AM) covers the exec summary for Block 2 automatically.
  • Block 2 (10-1 PM) is the 60-90 min execution block.
  • Optional Block 3 (evening) when scope demands — e.g. testing sessions, A2P submissions, IRS hold marathons.

✅ Tooling · Twin Mind live transcript + Claude HQ mid-call edits

  • Twin Mind writes the meeting transcript into chat with ~30-sec refresh / 2-3 min delay — no need to end the meeting to pull a transcript.
  • Unblocks: Claude HQ can edit the agent / dashboard / GHL config while the founders are still on the call.
  • Frankie reaction May 19 03:49: "You see 03:49 — it's two minutes delay. Wow. So you're going to — what? — it's in real time. Yeah, yeah, it's in real time."
  • Claude HQ access: already has Retell + GHL API tokens — can pull, edit, redeploy from a single prompt mid-call.
  • Net effect: the meeting is the work session.

🕔 Calendar / automation layer (queued to ship)

  • Block 1 invite: recurring 4:30 AM PT / 5:00 PM IST · Zoom link · pre-filled agenda template (yesterday recap → today plan → blockers → explicit owner).
  • Block 2 invite: hold 10 AM-1 PM PT / 10:30 PM-1:30 AM IST · tentative status · confirmed each morning during Block 1.
  • Notifications: Frankie wants alerts on top so the day doesn't drift — "I'll have my notifications, I'll have my alerts set up on it. We'll have automations on there."
  • Pre-block automation: Claude HQ auto-generates the previous-day summary + today's focus list 30 min before each block, dropped into both founders' WhatsApp.
  • Post-block automation: transcript pulled via Twin Mind → dashboard auto-updated → tasks added to Daily Tasks tab.

⚠ "Don't miss each other" — failure modes already burned

  • May 18: Chitraksh slept through agreed meet — "Bro I slept 😭". Frankie: "Your body needed it bro." — the schedule fix prevents this from recurring.
  • May 17-18: multiple "are you up?" pings on WhatsApp that didn't connect to a real meeting — the calendar slot replaces the WhatsApp coordination overhead.
  • Time-zone awareness: Chitraksh's parents available before 11 AM IST or after 8 PM IST · intro meet queued when Frankie picks.
  • Schedule debt: Frankie's day-job 5-9 AM PT carves the morning; "In Sync" blocks bracket it cleanly.

Voice AI · P1 · OUTBOUND v128 + INBOUND v15 LIVE on Retell (May 29)

May 29 · OUTBOUND v128 LIVE — opener reframe (Greetings part 2 STEP 1)

Agent agent_63a23bd2cc9273a9b4fea5656e + flow conversation_flow_96a5fd684b24. The STEP 1 opener was leading with a mortgage-protection mechanism lecture ("Mortgage protection is simple: you pay a small monthly premium…") AND asking for the appointment in the same breath — telegraphing the pitch, so cold 15-month-old leads bailed. Three surgical edits in the Greetings part 2 node (9,061 → 9,649 chars): (a) STEP 1 objective line — "position the APPOINTMENT" → build interest / get THEM asking questions / keep them talking; (b) "Say (…)" framing — mechanism-first → flag-first, no appt; (c) the spoken opener now LEADS with the property flag ("Your property on {{address}} came up flagged as having no mortgage protection on the loan with {{lender}}"), disarms the old lead, explicitly says "I'm not going to pitch you anything on this call," and ends with an open question. PATHs A–G, pain hook, NEPQ connector preserved — the appointment ask fires later, once they engage. Patch: retell/scripts/apply_opener_reframe_2026-05-29.py. Publish note: /publish-agent returns an empty 200 — v127 published, then a redundant retry republished identical content as v128 (live = v128, v127≡v128); new draft = v129.

INBOUND v16 — same reframe, drafted + HELD (not published). Agent agent_1ffc59c3d135d0776cb35fec6f + flow conversation_flow_302b435de58b. Adapted to the callback context: inbound has no dialer lead variables, so the flag is generic ("the mortgage on your home"); the greeting already says "thanks for calling back," so the opener says "thanks again for calling back… what had you call back?" 2 surgical edits (5,850 → 6,230 chars). Patch: retell/scripts/apply_inbound_opener_reframe_2026-05-29.py. Ships on "publish inbound".

🎤

May 28 · OUTBOUND v126 LIVE — email digit-word → numeric-digit fix shipped

Agent agent_63a23bd2cc9273a9b4fea5656e + flow conversation_flow_96a5fd684b24. v126 ships three surgical edits on top of v125: (a) global_prompt EMAIL CAPTURE — added a DIGITS bullet: when caller speaks digit words ("one"/"two"/"zero"/"oh"), convert to numerals (1/2/0) in the stored local-part; read each digit back individually ("one two" not "twelve"). Example: "john wick one two at gmail dot com" stores as johnwick12@gmail.com; read back "J. O. H. N. W. I. C. K. one two at gmail dot com". Negative example: NEVER spell digits as letters ("o. n. e. t. w. o."). (b) Node 9 (Identity Verification) email-capture — same DIGITS rule added to Format Rules + a worked example placed between the existing "j underscore 99" and "tony" examples (node text 4,090 → 4,847 chars). (c) post_call_analysis_data caller_email — extraction description extended (498 → 792 chars) with explicit digit-word → numeric-digit conversion table (zero/oh→0, one→1, …, nine→9) and the johnwick12 vs johnwickonetwo counterexample.

Inherited from v125 (still in v126): appointment_timestamp ISO 8601 spec (no n8n template syntax — LLM was previously falling back to natural-language strings that Google Calendar's create-event rejected with 400). callback_scheduled_time clarified as the human-readable companion to appointment_timestamp, preventing role confusion between the two callback-time variables. Patch script: retell/scripts/apply_email_digit_fix_2026-05-28.py. Snapshots: agent_pre_email_digit_fix_20260528_151544.json + post.

🏆

May 18 (Mon, 02:09-02:21) · VOICE "CREATURE" EXORCISED — 100% better on test call

The Maya/Tessa voice was producing a "creature" artifact mid-sentence (muffled syllables, partial words, breath clipping) on real outbound test calls; recording came back clean every time which told us it was a runtime transport issue, not a generation problem. Frankie: "Listen to it — whenever you... that's the perfect word, creatures." A live diagnostic session on the May 18 call ran the variables: first the voice was swapped (got worse), then the bug got isolated to Cartesia ↔ Retell transport (the voices are Cartesia imports, not native Retell, so retell-internal config wasn't the lever). Three fixes shipped in one pass: (a) voice volume +166 from default 100 — agent was simply too quiet for the cellphone codec to render its breath frames; (b) interruption-sensitivity dropped to floor — agent was treating its own breath / silence as a barge-in and clipping itself; (c) background-noise removal turned ON. Voice-speed toggle audit: was ON in two prompt nodes but OFF globally — brought all to OFF for consistency. Cartesia model swap: Sonic 3 → Sonic 3.5 — default was sticking to the older more-stable release; the newer experimental release turned out to be more stable in our case. Post-fix call verdict: "It's 100% better." — Frankie. Voice is keeper-at-any-cost; both founders aligned: "I like this voice, I want to save it at any cost."

🏆

May 18-19 · SALES-MASTER SCRIPT REBUILD · five GOATs merged into one prompt

With voice transport fixed, the script bottleneck surfaced: "It sounds robotic because it's a script, huh?" — Frankie. Decision: don't rewrite line-by-line in our weaker voices, instead let Claude HQ merge five sales GOATs into a single prompt. Jeremy Miner (NPQ — Neuro-Emotional Persuasion Questions: strip statements-as-questions, agent must ask real questions); Jordan Belfort (straight-line: tonality + control + framing the close); Chris Voss (tactical empathy + mirror + label); Andy Albright (mortgage-protection 30-day frame, "reason for the call is non-negotiable" — do not strip); Alex Hormozi (loss-aversion 2.5× — humans hate loss 2.5× more than they love gain · reframe to "family loses the house in 30 days" not "family gets a payment"). Trigger updated: death OR disabling illness / can't work (illness was missing in v1 — per the new transcript intake). Sam Lair upfront contract baked in: "If by the end of five minutes this isn't a fit, you'll tell me, you'll just tell me — deal? Frames the no. You can say it." Pitch bullet ordering locked: are-you-familiar-with-MP → (yes/no, same response: "no worries, most people don't") → explain trigger + payout → one / two / three / six-month time-to-decide → keep / rent / sell. Trim mortgage protection brief to: "If something happens to you, your beneficiary receives money right after you pass away to pay the mortgage so they don't lose the house" — then the time-frame ladder — then the disposition options.

✅ Voice fix · final config (May 18, locked)

  • Voice: Cartesia · Maya/Tessa import · keep at any cost.
  • Model: Cartesia Sonic 3.5 (up from Sonic 3).
  • Volume: +166 (was at default 100).
  • Interruption sensitivity: dropped to floor (was clipping own breath frames).
  • Background-noise removal: ON.
  • Voice-speed toggle: OFF on every node (was ON in 2 nodes, OFF in global).

🏆 Sales-master script · GOAT stack reference

  • Jeremy Miner · NPQ — no statements-as-questions, agent must ask real questions to surface emotion.
  • Jordan Belfort · straight-line — tonality + control + framing of the close.
  • Chris Voss · tactical empathy — mirror + label, accusations audit.
  • Andy Albright · mortgage-protection 30-day frame, "reason for the call is non-negotiable" — do not strip.
  • Alex Hormozi · loss-aversion 2.5× — "family loses the house in 30 days" framing replaces "family gets a payment".
  • Sam Lair · upfront contract — "if by 5 min this isn't a fit, you'll tell me, deal?".
  • Trigger: death OR disabling illness / can't work (illness was missing in v1).

⚡ Pitch bullet ordering (locked May 18)

  1. Open: "Hi, this is [Maya/Tessa] with Oraya Insurance Group. Am I speaking to [name]?" — "Am I speaking to" replaces the older "Did I get the right person" / "Hi this is X looking for Y" (Frankie note: "did I get the right person" sounds cold, "looking for" makes them defensive).
  2. Reason for call: truthful provenance — "we work with public homeowner records and lender databases, your loan came up with no mortgage protection on file."
  3. Permission to teach: "Are you familiar with how mortgage protection works?" — both yes and no route to the same teach (yes = "good, we'll run it to you briefly"; no = "no worries, most people don't, let me explain real quick").
  4. Trigger + payout: "If something happens to you — you pass away, or you can't work because of illness — mortgage protection kicks in. Your beneficiary — husband, wife, kids — receives money to pay the mortgage so they don't lose the house."
  5. Time-to-decide ladder: "They get one, two, three, six months — depending on the policy — to decide what they want to do."
  6. Disposition options: "Keep it, rent it, sell it. They're not forced into anything while they're grieving."
  7. Loss-aversion close (Hormozi): "Without it, family scrambles to make a decision on the house in 30 days. With it, they get months."
  8. Sam Lair contract: "If by the end of five minutes this isn't a fit, you'll just tell me — deal?"
  9. Book the appointment: explicit yes → calendar slot; soft no → one objection cycle → book or release.

🔎 Diagnostic SOP · voice + agent debug rules (post-May 18)

  • Symptom: "creature / muffled / clipping" mid-sentence on live calls but clean recording → transport-layer issue, not generation. Skip prompt-level debugging.
  • Check order: voice volume → interruption sensitivity → background-noise removal → voice-speed toggle parity across nodes → Cartesia model rev (3 vs 3.5) → only then retell-internal.
  • Don't: retry the same voice swap multiple times before checking transport. Don't blame the LLM unless transport is clean.
  • Don't: change voice when founders love it — voice is keeper-at-any-cost; tune transport around it.
  • Do: default to Cartesia's newer model rev when transport feels stale; older "stable" defaults can be the regression.
  • External validation: Frankie cross-checked against Google AI-mode while debugging — interruption sensitivity was the top suggestion (independent confirmation).

🧠 Single-prompt vs node-based · decision matrix

  • Node-based (current): easier per-step instruction, clearer fall-back logic, harder to feel "human" because each node has its own prompt — seams show.
  • Single-prompt (forked): harder to instrument step-by-step, easier to feel natural because the whole pitch lives in one place — agent owns the flow.
  • Risk: single-prompt is harder to convey step instructions to — Chitraksh's hedge: "if single-prompt is too difficult for us to convey to act upon, we continue with the node structure."
  • Decision: run both in parallel · A/B on real calls · choose by founder ear test · preserve loser as fallback for 30 days minimum.
  • Frankie: "50% chance it will be better than what we have already, right?" — bet sized correctly.

⚠ Pizza Hut "over-informing" lesson · apply to client dashboards

External signal logged May 18 02:33-02:43 — Pizza Hut $100M franchisee lawsuit over the Dragon Tail AI delivery system. Pizza Hut forced franchisees to adopt it; the AI exposed kitchen workflow timing (when each order would be ready) to DoorDash drivers. Drivers gamed it — clubbed 2-3-4 orders per pickup — food arrived cold — customer base eroded — revenue dropped ~1-2% YoY. Franchisees sued Pizza Hut for forcing the system + brand-damage. Frankie's framing: "That wasn't a software issue, that was an over-informing issue." Direct application: when Oraya ships client-side dashboards (dealership / insurance broker / franchisee), expose value, not the seams. Show: bookings, revenue, conversion. Hide: agent timing internals, raw transcript firehose, system-status latency that a counterparty could game. "Over-transparency is itself a system risk."

🔎

May 11-12 · Latency root-cause: 10s opening silence = first-node Sonnet

Symptom: agent opens with ~10 seconds of dead air before speaking. Models tested per-node: Sonnet on entry sounds clean but is too heavy (10s wake-up + cost), Haiku is cheap but introduces 10s+ delays on its own, GPT-5.5 fails the sales-tone test ("we got your form, life insurance, right?" stutter). Fix being shipped: lighter / cached model on the entry node, Sonnet on the hand-off node where reasoning matters. Cadence target backed by the May 13 FTO research: 150-300ms response gap, ~200ms universal baseline; humans predict end-of-sentence at 600-1500ms cognitive lag and start formulating mid-sentence — we model that pre-emption. Final test pass scheduled with Frankie this week; agent goes back live as soon as it passes.

Sales-prompt guardrails · 4 rules

#RuleOrigin quote
G1No-skip-qualification: even after user says "test drive," do NOT jump to first-name/email capture. Ask current vehicle + what they want different + model suggestion first."It skipped the sales and inventory node entirely"
G2Contextual sales: after user names current car, use it. EV → ask EV vs gas. Family car → family-oriented. Performance → AMG line. Never collect data without using it."What's the point of asking the information if you're not going to know what to do with it"
G3Assume add, not replace: Mercedes customers often add to collection. Reframe: "are you looking to add a Mercedes to the lineup?""I love my car, why am I switching it up"
G4Never offer email-breakdown as alternative to appointment. Kills conversion. Only "come see it in person" closes."Some people are going to say give me a fucking email and then we killed our own appointment"
v9 inventory rebuild spec (R13 · paste-ready, pre-pilot)

v3 synonym JSON covering 12 families, 72 trims. Families: S, E, C, CLE, SL, AMG-GT, GLA, GLB, GLC, GLE, GLS, G, EQB, EQE, EQS, Sprinter. Utterance normaliser plus 35-case Node test harness plus Supabase verdict SQL (Q1-Q4). Deploy path: set FAMILY_MAP env, deploy Code node, swap Supabase query to .in('trim', trimArray), wire empty branch to respond-to-webhook.

Frankie's origin quote: "The reason why they call it a S-Class is because there's so many different type of specs. S500, S580, S580E, S560. No one knows the name of these specs but a lot of people know if they want an S-Class. But the DB doesn't have S-Class in the names. That's where it's having a difficult time."

Diagnostic SQL (R13 verdict): Q1 total count, Q2 S-Class variant count (where trim ~ '^S[0-9]{3}'), Q3 cron freshness (max(updated_at)), Q4 2026 model-year coverage. Q2=0 means sync-miss. Q2>0 and Q4<dealer-site-count means query-tool fault. Q3 age > 24h means cron failing.

Mortgage-Protection Agent v1.0 · persona + 3 pitch tracks (May 5-6 spec)

Refactored from generic life-insurance Maya into a dedicated mortgage-protection agent. Persona is anchored to the Apr 28 sales coaching that opened "we work with banks like [their lender]" — truth-first, no fake "you filled out a form a year ago" framing. Frankie's locked instruction: "Eliminate any deception from the gate. We're standing firm. We pulled mortgage records, we saw you don't have coverage, we have relationships with multiple carriers, we can shop them at one time."

Greeting open (every call)

  • Truthful provenance line: "We work with banks like [their lender], plus a couple of others. We pulled mortgage records and public information for homeowners with active loans, and we saw you don't have coverage in place. We can shop multiple carriers at once and lock in the best rate."
  • Why "like": the first bank named is the lead's actual lender (from the dynamic variable), then 2-3 more so the prospect can't say "you don't work with my bank" and disqualify the truth claim.
  • Then qualify: "Is it important to you to leave this house with less debt or more debt? That's the only thing I need to know — if it's important, I can put a licensed advisor in front of you for 10-15 minutes."

Three pitch tracks (assigned by Lead Recovery Matrix)

TrackTrigger row signalsPitch postureCarrier framing
Elite RiskAge 30s-40s, clean health profile, high mortgage, no tobacco"You're in our top tier pricing bracket. The catch — this rate is age-locked. Every birthday it goes up."Mortgage protection inside your loan = peace of mind for the family; pure protection, $15-30/mo for a healthy applicant
Medical ConditionDisclosed asthma / blood pressure / diabetes / chronic condition in rowCarriers who specifically underwrite medical conditions; protection-focused, not investment-shapedBaltimore Life / similar conditional-issue carriers; standard issue if eligibility
Tobacco UserTobacco = yes in row"We have carriers who actively insure smokers with shields and bands tailored to that profile."Tobacco-friendly carriers; reframe pricing as protection, not penalty

Dynamic variables seeded per row

Name · phone · lender bank · mortgage amount · address · city · co-borrower (yes/no) · borrower age · medical condition · tobacco use. The agent uses these inline (not just at intro) — Frankie observed: "without us telling it, it can use those informations in between conversation also."

Pricing-statement guardrail (May 6 fix)

Maya quoted "$15-30 a month" without distinguishing term from whole life, which would create a bait-and-switch when an agent quotes higher for permanent coverage. Updated prompt: any pricing reference must say "for the most affordable option, like a term policy, around $15-30 a month." Cross-product positioning: "think of term as your starting point right now; once budget allows, we can layer in a whole-life or cash-value piece on next year's annual review." Never bash whole life or cash value (we sell those too).

Closing pattern (mortgage-protection specific)

Reframe life insurance vs. mortgage protection: "life insurance is for your burial and your family's immediate bills, but your mortgage needs to be protected separately so that when you pass, your wife or kids get a check each month from the carrier paying the mortgage. They get time — 6 to 9 months — to decide whether to keep the house, sell, rent. You buy them time." That story is the agent's one-shot to break "I already have life insurance" objection.

Lead Recovery Matrix · 132 homeowners (May 5)

Google-Sheets-AI-agent intelligence layer over Teresa's mortgage-protection lead list. For each row it scores risk bucket (Elite / Medical / Tobacco), strategic-insight notes, and emits the dynamic-variable bundle for Maya. Frankie reaction on the live walk-through: "Wait a minute. Oh my gosh. This is a product in itself, bro. What the fuck are you doing over there. You are crazy. This is wild."

  • 132 homeowners qualified for mortgage protection out of the active list — the universe Maya runs against in the first outbound batch.
  • Strategic insights are written column-by-column per row; each row gets a personalized pitch reading even before the agent dials.
  • Risk-bucket coloring: Elite Risk = green (best state); Medical = amber; Tobacco = red (most acute pitch posture). Coloring is for the operator, not the agent.
  • Reusable to scale: the same Google-Sheets agent runs against any new mortgage-protection list ingested into the system — one-time engineering, infinite leverage.
  • Pulls into Maya prompt: the row's dynamic variables are surfaced as conversation context. Frankie observation: agent uses them inline, not just at intro — "a lot of people might get personalized information in between the questions that they ask and we did not even prompt to do it."

George Morrison RPA debrief (May 1) · 2-agent pattern confirmed

Frankie + Teresa walked the Baltimore Life pre-app live with George Morrison + Vanessa, Chitraksh observing for the RPA spec. Verified pattern for production carrier auto-fill:

  • Carrier flow length: ~5-10 minutes wall-clock once the pre-app form is up — vs. ~40-60 minutes for a non-instant carrier (e.g. Mutual of Omaha referred-to-underwriting path).
  • Inputs that matter for instant approval: last-4 SSN + DOB + height/weight + tobacco status + driver's license + address + checking account + routing. Identity-verify uses last-4 only and rejects fast (kicks back "unable to verify client" if anything mismatched).
  • Two signature gates: (1) at the start to authorize medical look-up; (2) at the end to submit. Both are link-driven (text/email) — the user clicks "adopt and sign" then "finish/submit."
  • Approval signal: Baltimore Life returns "preferred non-tobacco" or modified status within ~2 seconds of identity-verify pass — pivot decision happens immediately, not after underwriting cycle.
  • 2-agent RPA spec: agent A handles the carrier portal (form fields, signature link triggers, submission); agent B holds the call (talks to the customer, asks the next question, narrates the wait). They sync on a shared state machine because there are gaps between SMS sent and signature received.
  • Carrier discipline rule: pick 3 carriers and stick — charge-back exposure on a one-off carrier you can't write-over kills the unit-economics.

Production queue: 2-agent build sits behind Boatman go-live. Once paid-ads inbound starts hitting Frankie's calendar, George-class closes are the proving ground for the auto-fill agent.

Pricing and unit economics

  • Entry · $997/mo · voice AI baseline, single location.
  • Growth · $3-5K/mo/location · full stack + SLA, post-pilot.
  • Enterprise · $7-11K/mo/location · custom + inventory AI.
  • Pilot · 30 days / $0 platform fee / 24h exit / 72h data purge.
  • Insurance · $25-50/lead · $50-100/appt · $1K/wk retainer · 140% commission ($1,920/policy).
  • Hybrid billing (Apr 22 LOCK): flat rate + usage-based. Per-seat / per-dealership fixed line + Retell minute pass-through. Stripe meter configured (display API, event request).

Unit economics: $997 at $30-40 infra equals approx 96% gross. $5K tier is effectively pure margin.

Public-mortgage-data lead pipeline · HOF Leads model decoded (May 7)

Closed the research from May 3 + May 7. Asked the RPA to reverse-engineer how Hall of Fame Leads (hofleads.com) sells mortgage-protection leads — turns out the model is simpler than expected.

HOF Leads canonical method

  • Pulls public-data sources (county recorder office: deed + lender name + mortgage amount + new-house address) plus premium data sources (CoreLogic / Atom / Property Shark for filtered "recent sales by lender + loan amount").
  • Enriches the cold rows via Apollo or equivalent enrichment for phone/email (the row from county records doesn't carry phone/email, only name + address + lender + amount).
  • Sends a physical mailer to the homeowner's new address in an envelope styled like a bank letter ("our records indicate your loan with [Bank] may need attention — respond by [date]").
  • Mailer routes to an 800 IVR — voluntary disclosure of DOB / height/weight / smoker / health condition. Anyone who completes it becomes an opt-in lead.
  • Postage is the only meaningful cost (~$0.30-0.50/letter). Margins survive because each completed lead converts at ~$3-10K AP commissions.

Oraya's adaptation

  • Skip postage entirely. Cold-email + voice + LinkedIn DM the same opt-in pattern. Postage stays a "future option" only if the email/voice path under-performs.
  • HTTP-request enrichment chain keyed off (state, name, age) per row: county records pull → CoreLogic / Property Shark / Atom (whichever exposes the lender filter) → TruePeopleSearch for phone/email. Same recipe as the inventory enrichment we built for Mercedes.
  • Manual fallback documented: truepeoplesearch.com works as the human verification step when the automated enrichment misses on a high-priority row.
  • Conversion math (CEO ballpark): even if we land 5-10 extra sales/month from this pipeline at $1-2K each = covers Oraya's monthly subscription stack. Sub-vertical ROI is positive at any non-zero conversion.

Lead scoring + exhaustion cadence · CTO-Claude answer (Apr 24)

Frankie's ask: "ay, 9th day, 15th day etc, i think 2 weeks is sufficient but could be wrong, we will ask HQ what is optimal amount of time to lead exhaustion simultaneously reducing costs for leads less likely to convert, add lead scoring so only the hottest leads go to appointments based on buying signals + intent analyzed by our AI."

Verdict: Frankie's 2-week instinct is right for the MIDDLE tier — but a flat 2-week cap burns hot leads and keeps dead leads alive too long. A scored + tiered cadence is the right structure.

Proposed cadence (by score tier)

ScoreTierTouchesCadenceExhaustionChannel
≥ 70Hot5 touchesDay 0, 1, 3, 5, 9Day 10 → nurtureVoice AI call + SMS + email
40-69Warm6 touchesDay 0, 2, 5, 9, 15, 21Day 22 → nurtureEmail + SMS · voice only on reply
< 40Cold3 touchesDay 0, 7, 21Day 22 → nurtureEmail only · no Retell minutes
Any (nurture)Long tailQuarterlyD+60, D+90, D+180Permanent drop at D+365Email only

Cost containment logic: only Hot (score ≥ 70) leads get expensive Retell minutes after touch #1. Warm leads earn Retell time only after a positive reply. Cold leads are email-only — cost per touch drops from ~$0.42/call to ~$0.001/email, a 420x reduction on the bottom 60% of the pipeline.

Scoring dimensions (AI-derived, 0-100)

DimensionWeightSignalSource
Explicit ask25"Send me a quote" > "Tell me more" > generic interest > no askRetell transcript NLP
Response latency15<1hr (25pt), <24hr (15pt), <72hr (7pt), >72hr (0pt)Supabase timestamps
Conversation length15≥3 min voice (15pt), 1-3 min (8pt), <1 min (0pt)Retell call duration
Specificity15Named coverage type + dollar amount mentioned = full pointsTranscript NLP
Quote / calendar Q15Asked for quote or appointment = full pointsIntent classifier
Demographic fit10Age + state + prior-policy match carrier appetiteApollo enrichment
Reply sentiment5Positive > neutral > negativeTranscript NLP

Routing rules (on each touch outcome)

  • Score jumps ≥ 15 points on any touch → upgrade tier immediately; live-agent handoff within 5 minutes for Hot.
  • Two consecutive silent touches at Warm or Cold → demote one tier.
  • Explicit "do not contact" or hard unsubscribe → permanent DNC list, zero further touches (TCPA + CAN-SPAM + CA SB 1001 compliance).
  • Appointment booked → freeze automated sequence, hand to Frankie or qualified agent.
  • No-show on booked appointment → drop one tier + schedule recovery sequence at Day +3.

Why this beats flat 2-week

  • Hot leads get 5 touches in 9 days rather than 3 in 14 — no oxygen lost to a policy buyer who's ready NOW.
  • Cold leads get 3 email touches over 21 days at pennies, not 3 voice calls at $1.26 of Retell burn.
  • Nurture tail captures leads that convert at 6-12 month decision cycles (common in life insurance) at quarterly email cost, ~$0.003 each.
  • Compliance is encoded in routing, not bolted on — DNC, unsubscribe, appointment-freeze are all rule-driven, audit-traceable.

Infra to build (Chitraksh queue): scoring function in n8n (reads Supabase lead_events + Retell transcript NLP output), writes back score, tier, next_touch_at columns. Cadence scheduler fires from next_touch_at triggers. Dashboard adds a Lead Pipeline tab (future v11) with tier breakdown + cost-per-appointment KPI.

Sequencing: score function + scheduler = ~2 days of n8n + Supabase work for Chitraksh; ship BEFORE the first paid-ads test campaign lands, so the inbound lead flow hits a live scoring engine instead of a flat cadence.

Legal · In-house AI Legal Stack · A2P + IPA + FBN + multi-model audit

⚖

May 12-17 · A2P document pack drafted + cross-verified across 4 AI models · 7-8 laws in scope

Claude ran the legal audit on the Oraya Insurance Group A2P package and then cross-verified the result across 4 other AI models to catch gaps before the regulator does. The audit closed on 7-8 laws in scope: California Consumer Privacy Act / CPRA, federal privacy (TCPA, CAN-SPAM, FCC robocall rules), California Insurance Information Practices Act (IPA), California SB 1001 (bot disclosure), CIPA two-party recording, SB 446 (72-hour breach), FTC § 5, with the binding principle: "ignorance of law is not an excuse." Two new structural requirements surfaced from the audit and were both folded into the package: (1) a Fictitious Business Name (FBN) filing for Oraya Insurance Group in California — required because operating + registering the brand under a name that isn't the legal entity name is a deemed FBN; (2) explicit California IPA notice on the lead-capture form (carrier discovery, what data we collect, how the agent uses it, how to opt out). The whole pack ships as: Terms of Service, Privacy Policy, California IPA Notice, Master Service Agreement (MSA), AI-generated voice + automated message disclosure, message-frequency disclosure (~8 SMS + 4 calls per month), opt-in form with the disclosures inline — all built and ready to submit the moment Oraya's EIN lands.

Multi-model audit method · the "n+4" verification SOP

The audit pattern that landed during the May 12 meeting is now an SOP: Claude drafts the legal pack → Claude runs a structural audit against the in-scope statute list → the audit + draft are then cross-verified across 4 other AI models (different vendors / different training distributions). Disagreements between models surface specific clauses that need a human read or a citation check; consensus across all 5 models is treated as ready-to-ship. The pattern caught both the FBN gap and the IPA-notice gap on this package — neither was obvious from the GHL Trust Center walk-through alone. Reusable across vertical packs (dealership, real-estate, dental). Pairs with the in-house in-house external-counsel trigger list below: anything the 5-model audit flags as ambiguous is escalated; anything it agrees on ships.

Rec A · CALL IRS TONIGHT until EIN is issued

Play: Frankie + Chitraksh on a joint call (Frankie speaks, Chitraksh narrates the SS-4 fields), keep redialling the IRS Business & Specialty Tax line (1-800-829-4933) until the EIN is read out. Have SS-4 fields pre-filled. Backup: file SS-4 via fax for guaranteed 4-business-day turnaround as a parallel path so we are never single-threaded.

Why: EIN is the only blocker between us and submitting the A2P brand. Every day of slip is a day AutoNation outbound stays gated and a day insurance leads can’t be texted at A2P-rate throughput.

Owner: Frankie + Chitraksh · Timing: Sun May 17 evening — tonight.

Rec B · Submit A2P brand + campaign the moment EIN lands

Play: with the package pre-built (terms, privacy, IPA, MSA, AI-voice + frequency disclosure, opt-in), open the GHL Trust Center, paste EIN, pay $24, submit brand. Once brand verifies (instant), submit campaign. Track AI-checklist verdict + regulator queue status daily.

Psychographic Profiles · May 19 snapshot

May 17-19 partnership signals (new this sweep)

  • "In Sync" naming logic exposes a founder asset thesis. Frankie May 19 03:44: "Have you ever heard of a music group called *NSYNC, the American music group? They were when I was a kid. The name In Sync is very marketable, very very very high leverage once you get there." — the schedule isn't just a schedule; it's a reserved brand surface and a positioning narrative for how two-person AI-only companies actually operate. Frankie's instinct is to find leverage in names; this is the second time it has surfaced (Oraya itself).
  • Schedule = the love language. The whole point of the In Sync schedule is the absence of friction. Frankie May 19 03:44: "If me and you could be in sync with each other in our schedules — we don't miss each other anymore." — not "we will be more productive," not "we will move faster." The frame is "don't miss each other". Healthy founder pair.
  • Failure modes named without shame on both sides. Chitraksh May 18: "Bro I slept 😭" after missing the agreed meet. Frankie: "Your body needed it bro." — no scoring, no leverage, no "make it up." Same beat as the Apr 25 forgotten-haircut moment. Mature pair pattern.
  • External news intake is shared and same-direction. May 18 Frankie reads the Meta-employees-tracked-to-build-replacement headline and pings "Bro · Bro · Bro"; Chitraksh: "Everything we read makes us feel better about our choices." Two days later: Pizza Hut $100M, Pope+AI, Anthropic moral compass — same pattern. The shared interpretive frame is what keeps morale stable through dips.
  • Voice-fix collaboration was actually collaboration. Frankie May 18 ~02:46: "I swear to God I wasn't even doing a deep research, I'm just on Google AI mode · it told me that was one of the things it suggested, but I didn't want to tell you because I think you're the person that's in control of the system." Chitraksh: "Sometimes the problem is right in front of your eyes and you are over-complicating it." Both founders independently converged on the interruption-sensitivity fix; Frankie's restraint about not pre-empting Chitraksh's diagnostic is a high-trust move.
  • Direct, blunt creative critique is the working register. May 18 voice-test verdicts — "Now it sounds robotic", "It's getting cut in between", "the perfect word, creatures", "You're fucking fire. This is great." — no padding, no hedging, no "what do you think." Useful for compressed cycle time.
  • Money conversations are matter-of-fact. May 18 04:00: Frankie's card charged $100-120 for Claude Max · Chitraksh proposes downgrade to $30 + $30 multi-vendor · Frankie: "Either way it's fine because we'll not let those tokens get wasted." No defensiveness about who pays, no scoring. Capacity-not-cost framing.
  • Drake / Kendrick tangent (May 18 03:05-03:16) — 11 minutes of culture talk inside a script-rebuild meeting. Frankie self-aware: "You know what I was just thinking, our system is going to blast us in the dashboard for this conversation right now. But it's fine. We can change it." Then immediately: "I'm ready." Pattern: the founders take the breath, then snap back. Don't reduce the tangent budget — it's where alignment gets refreshed.
  • Frankie's analytical reflex is intact even on tangents. Same Drake conversation: he refuses to dunk on Drake purely on tribal grounds; runs the analysis evenhandedly; ends on "His album is mid anyways. And that's what hurts my feelings to say." The same reflex he uses to read the Pizza Hut lawsuit ("that wasn't a software issue, that was an over-informing issue") and the Suleyman forecast. He doesn't outsource judgment.
  • Family + faith come back as decision filters. May 18 02:06: Chitraksh on Anthropic moral-compass hiring — "I even thought it like six, seven months ago I thought that when AI gets to a point where it's conscious enough to take decisions, it should be religious enough to have at least a moral compass." Frankie's parallel reaction to the Pope-AI guidelines news. Shared instinct: AI without ethical grounding is the failure mode; both founders treat that as a system risk, not a philosophical sidebar.
  • Frankie protects Chitraksh's family time. May 19 03:48: "At that time usually my family is going up to sleep. So sometimes I might need to attend to them — let's not fix that one." Frankie immediately accepts: "Yeah, yeah. Okay let's keep it flexible." Block 2 stays floating specifically to protect Chitraksh's evening-family overlap.

May 10-17 partnership signals (preserved)

  • Brotherhood as operating norm. Chitraksh told his parents about Frankie and Oraya seriousness this week; Frankie's reply (May 17): "I am excited to meet them brother and honored." Family-introduction is now part of the founder pact, not a future event.
  • Boundaries respected without performative hand-wringing. Frankie May 10 (Mother's Day): "Today is mother's day in my country. I'm gonna be with my moms and my daughters mom — I am available for a phone call to catch up but not on laptop today brother." Chitraksh: "Okay brother no worries. Take your time." Same pattern when Chitraksh asked to defer to morning before his last exam — Frankie: "As you should. I trust your judgment 100%."
  • Direct critical feedback in real time. During the May 10-11 voice A/B Frankie's verbatim feedback was harsh by design: "That shit sounds stupid right now bro. Bro is special lmao. Ok this one seems slow as fuck. Like mentally disabled. All them ask questions like a statement — I hate that." Chitraksh absorbed it without flinching, iterated until "Tessa hired" landed. The pair has the trust to be that blunt without breakage.
  • Shared reframing under load. Both founders read the same external news the same way. May 17 Mustafa Suleyman quote, Chitraksh: "Everything we read makes us feel better about our choices." Frankie: "My inclination is correct, as yours is as well. The world is transforming in front of our eyes." Same map; identical reading.
  • Capacity expansion is the headline pattern of the week. Frankie shipped the Sales SOP + 30-min demo + payment-collection script on May 11 (becomes SOP for him today and the future sales team). Chitraksh moved home + set up the spare-room Oraya office + went 24/7. Together they wrote a multi-agent CEO stack so the next 5x of throughput doesn't require either of them adding hours.
  • Compliance bias is mutual. Both founders accepted the 5-model legal audit recommendation (FBN + IPA + privacy disclosures) without push-back. "Ignorance of law is not an excuse" was logged as a founder principle, not a footnote.

Founder archetype · Visionary Hustler + Systems-First Operator

Frankie is a natural-born entrepreneur: relationship-first, intuitive about human psychology, real domain expertise in automotive + insurance, high EQ. Origin of "Oraya" is Hebrew for "light of God" — chosen while pursuing Uzi Sassoon (Jewish, Samsung sale). Views the company as a calling, not coincidence. Faith framing surfaces in meetings: "we're brothers bro, God brought us together." Comms style: long stream-of-consciousness, analogies, profanity equals warmth. Positive signals: "Say less," "Yesir," "Let's cook," "Fire," "Bet," "That's crazy bro." Negative: silence or sudden one-word replies. AI directive (Mtg 16, verbatim): "I want our AI to end up working with our personalities, more ChatGPT understanding, a little looser, less rigid with us, personally, not for less accountability but for more flexibility and interaction instead of just reading like fucking lines."

Frankie strengths: world-class sales instinct; exceptional relationship capital (owners with 50-100 person teams; "one-to-two intros from insurance billionaires"); wide visionary range (Quote AI + DAO + Holding Co held for 2+ years); deep insurance domain (IUL traps, carrier dynamics, chargebacks, CPL econ, commission structures); high EQ with authentic gratitude and warm disagreement; rare Apr 19 superpower — social-cue-to-engineering-bug translation (when a call "feels weird" he can map that to a specific flow bug before CTO opens the workflow). Growth areas: focus/topic discipline (tangential 20-min stories before returning to point); task-tracking anxiety ("update my fucking execution and task completion rate"); scope slips (paystub favor was the Apr 19 incident, mutually closed). Motivations: legacy + money ("change insurance the way Waymo changed transportation"), God's timing, proving himself (non-technical, jail history, "it doesn't matter"), freedom for Chitraksh (wants him in US once profitable).

Chitraksh is CTO + law background + multi-surface builder. Systems abstraction, ships fast, refuses rebuilds, 9 parallel workstreams. Max-autonomy expectation: auto-learn, auto-act, no permission-asking on routine tasks. Comms: direct, no fluff, zero tolerance for em dashes (signals AI-generated content). Dark-theme HTML briefings, not markdown. Positive: "on it," "understood," "I'll do that," "check this out," "okay bro." Negative: silence or re-asked context (= frustration trigger).

Chitraksh strengths: deep stack across Retell (built CTO Copilot), n8n (86-workflow library), Supabase, Twilio A2P 10DLC, Next.js/Vercel; India common-law + CA + federal legal training; production-first mindset, hates over-planning, ships fast; proactive (if doable now, already in motion); new Apr 19 strength live root-cause diagnosis under load (three distinct bugs identified in-session, not post-mortem). Growth areas: context-switching load (9 projects); risk appetite leans aggressive (killed Strategy Law $10K retainer same hour he heard the price); delegation pattern still forming. Anti-patterns to avoid: rebuilding from scratch, over-explaining Retell/n8n basics, asking permission on routine tasks, losing context between sessions, clinical/corporate tone, any dash variant, accepting non-Oraya favor work. Apr 19 heuristic: when Chitraksh says "now now it involves an it-in, it's not just a prompt," the fix has crossed from configuration into architecture — scope-gate it.

Pairing dynamics: Frankie names the failure in human-language, Chitraksh maps it to the node + file — same call. Mtg 19 cleanest example in 14 weeks: Frankie said "she tried to book an appointment after I asked her about the car," Chitraksh immediately said "it skipped the sales and inventory node entirely." That cycle turned an hour of guessing into three fixes. Same-call loop-closure beats async tickets. Every major fix has happened inside a live meeting, not a handoff document. Gating: Frankie gates demos (vetoed demoing inventory to Teresa), Chitraksh gates architecture (vetoed shipping inventory to Tuesday). Both calls were right and neither was re-litigated. Format: phone outperforms screen-share. Decisions/min and tangent ratio both better. Shared anti-pattern: scope-creep favors for friends/family (paystub was shared failure mode; new pact surfaced naturally).

CTO/CLO Master Brief · 90-second exec read · May 19

Where we are May 19 — one paragraph

Oraya closed "Voice-Fix + Sales-Master Week."
